       \"valid values: line, block, class_body, function_body, function_signature, braces, brackets, parens\",\n   570\t        )),\n   571\t    }\n   572\t}\n   573\t\n   574\tfn parse_position(value: Option<&str>, index: usize, source: &Path) -> Result<Position, JigError> {\n   575\t    match value {\n   576\t        None | Some(\"after\") => Ok(Position::After),\n   577\t        Some(\"before\") => Ok(Position::Before),\n   578\t        Some(\"before_close\") => Ok(Position::BeforeClose),\n   579\t        Some(\"after_last_field\") => Ok(Position::AfterLastField),\n   580\t        Some(\"after_last_method\") => Ok(Position::AfterLastMethod),\n   581\t        Some(\"after_last_import\") => Ok(Position::AfterLastImport),\n   582\t        Some(\"sorted\") => Ok(Position::Sorted),\n   583\t        Some(other) => Err(recipe_err(\n   584\t            &format!(\"invalid 'position' value: '{other}'\"),\n   585\t            &format!(\"files[{index}] in {}\", source.display()),\n   586\t            \"position must be one of: before, after, before_close, after_last_field, after_last_method, after_last_import, sorted\",\n   587\t            \"valid values: before, after, before_close, after_last_field, after_last_method, after_last_import, sorted\",\n   588\t        )),\n   589\t    }\n   590\t}\n   591\t\n   592\tfn recipe_err(what: &str, where_: &str, why: &str, hint: &str) -> JigError {\n   593\t    JigError::RecipeValidation(StructuredError {\n   594\t        what: what.to_string(),\n   595\t        where_: where_.to_string(),\n   596\t 132\t/// Character-by-character scanner over lines.\n   133\tstruct CharScanner<'a> {\n   134\t    lines: &'a [&'a str],\n   135\t    line: usize,\n   136\t    col: usize,\n   137\t}\n   138\t\n   139\timpl<'a> CharScanner<'a> {\n   140\t    fn new(lines: &'a [&'a str], line: usize, col: usize) -> Self {\n   141\t        Self { lines, line, col }\n   142\t    }\n   143\t\n   144\t    fn normalize(&mut self) {\n   145\t        while self.line < self.lines.len() {\n   146\t            let line_len = self.lines[self.line].chars().count();\n   147\t            if self.col < line_len {\n   148\t                return;\n   149\t            }\n   150\t            self.line += 1;\n   151\t            self.col = 0;\n   152\t        }\n   153\t    }\n   154\t\n   155\t    fn peek(&mut self) -> Option<char> {\n   156\t        self.normalize();\n   157\t        if self.line >= self.lines.len() {\n   158\t            return None;\n   159\t        }\n   160\t        self.lines[self.line].chars().nth(self.col)\n   161\t    }\n   162\t\n   163\t    fn peek_next(&mut self) -> Option<char> {\n   164\t        self.normalize();\n   165\t        if self.line >= self.lines.len() {\n   166\t            return None;\n   167\t        }\n   168\t        let line_len = self.lines[self.line].chars().count();\n   169\t        if self.col + 1 < line_len {\n   170\t            self.lines[self.line].chars().nth(self.col + 1)\n   171\t        } else if self.line + 1 < self.lines.len() && !self.lines[self.line + 1].is_empty() {\n   172\t            self.lines[self.line + 1].chars().next()\n   173\t        } else {\n   174\t            None\n   175\t        }\n   176\t    }\n   177\t\n   178\t    fn advance(&mut self) {\n   179\t        if self.line >= self.lines.len() {\n   180\t            return;\n   181\t        }\n   182\t        let line_len = self.lines[self.line].chars().count();\n   183\t        self.col += 1;\n   184\t        if self.col >= line_len {\n   185\t            self.line += 1;\n   186\t            self.col = 0;\n   187\t        }\n   188\t    }\n   189\t\n   190\t    fn skip_string_literal(&mut self, quote: char) {\n   191\t        self.advance(); // Skip opening quote.\n   192\t        loop {\n   193\t            match self.peek() {\n   194\t                None => return, // Unterminated string — bail.\n   195\t                Some('\\\\') => {\n   196\t                    self.advance(); // Skip backslash.\n   197\t                    self.advance(); // Skip escaped character.\n   198\t                }\n   199\t                Some(ch) if ch == quote => {\n   200\t                    self.advance(); // Skip closing quote.\n   201\t                    return;\n   202\t                }\n   203\t                _ => self.advance(),\n   204\t            }\n   205\t        }\n   206\t    }\n   207\t\n   208\t    fn skip_line_comment(&mut self) {\n   209\t        // Skip to end of line.\n   210\t        if self.line < self.lines.len() {\n   211\t            self.line += 1;\n   212\t            self.col = 0;\n   213\t        }\n   214\t    }\n   215\t\n   216\t    fn skip_block_comment(&mut self) {\n   217\t        self.advance(); // Skip '/'\n   218\t        self.advance(); // Skip '*'\n   219\t        loop {\n   220\t            match self.peek() {\n   221\t                None => return,\n   222\t                Some('*') => {\n   223\t                    if self.peek_next() == Some('/') {\n   224\t                        self.advance(); // Skip '*'\n   225\t                        self.advance(); // Skip '/'\n   226\t                        return;\n   227\t                    }\n   228\t                    self.advance();\n   229\t                }\n   230\t                _ => self.advance(),\n   231\t            }\n   232\t        }\n   233\t    }\n   234\t}\n   235\t\n   236\t// ── Tests m.insert(\"inject\".into(), serde_json::Value::String(inject.clone()));\n   408\t            }\n   409\t            recipe::FileOp::Replace { replace, .. } => {\n   410\t                m.insert(\"replace\".into(), serde_json::Value::String(replace.clone()));\n   411\t            }\n   412\t            recipe::FileOp::Patch { patch, .. } => {\n   413\t                m.insert(\"patch\".into(), serde_json::Value::String(patch.clone()));\n   414\t            }\n   415\t        }\n   416\t        serde_json::Value::Object(m)\n   417\t    }).collect();\n   418\t\n inject_count = 0usize;\n   431\t    let mut replace_count = 0usize;\n   432\t    let mut patch_count = 0usize;\n   433\t    for op in &recipe.files {\n   434\t        match op {\n   435\t            recipe::FileOp::Create { .. } => create_count += 1,\n   436\t            recipe::FileOp::Inject { .. } => inject_count += 1,\n   437\t            recipe::FileOp::Replace { .. } => replace_count += 1,\n   438\t            recipe::FileOp::Patch { .. } => patch_count += 1,\n   439\t        }\n   440\t    }\n   441\t    let mut parts = Vec::new();\n   442\t    if create_count > 0 {\n   443\t        parts.push(format!(\"{create_count} create\"));\n   444\t    }\n   445\t    if inject_count > 0 {\n   446\t        parts.push(format!(\"{inject_count} inject\"));\n   447\t    }\n   448\t    if replace_count > 0 {\n   449\t        parts.push(format!(\"{replace_count} replace\"));\n   450\t    }\n   451\t    if patch_count > 0 {\n   452\t        parts.push(format!(\"{patch_count} patch\"));\n   453\t    }\n   454\t    if parts.is_empty() {\n   455\t        \"none\".to_string()\n   456\t    } else {\n   457\t        parts.join(\", \")\n   458\t    }\n   459\t}\n   460\t\n where_: format!(\"{}{}\", template_name, line_info),\n   141\t        why: detail.to_string(),\n   142\t        hint: \"check Jinja2 syntax — ensure all blocks are properly closed\".into(),\n   143\t    })\n   144\t}\n   145\t\n   146\t/// Find the undefined variable in a template by scanning for references\n   147\t/// not present in the variable context.\n   148\t///\n   149\t/// Limitation: this is a best-effort heuristic using regex. It extracts only the\n   150\t/// first identifier from expressions like `{{ user.name }}` (yields \"user\", not\n   151\t/// \"user.name\"). Falls back to \"unknown\" if no match is found. minijinja does not\n   152\t/// expose the undefined variable name directly, so this is the best we can do for v0.1.\n   153\tfn find_undefined_variable(template_source: &str, error_line: Option<usize>, vars: &Value) -> String {\n   154\t    let var_keys: Vec<&str> = match vars.as_object() {\n   155\t        Some(obj) => obj.keys().map(|s| s.as_str()).collect(),\n   156\t        None => vec![],\n   157\t    };\n   158\t\n   159\t    // Extract variable references from the template.\n   160\t    // Matches {{ name }}, {{ name | filter }}, {{ name.attr }}, etc.\n   161\t    let re = regex::Regex::new(r\"\\{\\{[\\s-]*([a-zA-Z_][a-zA-Z0-9_]*)\").unwrap();\n   162\t    // Also check {% if/for/elif blocks\n   163\t    let block_re = regex::Regex::new(r\"\\{%[\\s-]*(?:if|elif|for\\s+\\w+\\s+in|set\\s+\\w+\\s*=)\\s+([a-zA-Z_][a-zA-Z0-9_]*)\").unwrap();\n   164\t\n   165\t    let lines: Vec<&str> = template_source.lines().collect();\n   166\t\n   167\t    // If we have a line number, check that line first\n   168\t    if let Some(line_num) = error_line.filter(|&l| l > 0 && l <= lines.len()) {\n   169\t        let line = lines[line_num - 1];\n   170\t        for cap in re.captures_iter(line).chain(block_re.captures_iter(line)) {\n   171\t            let name = &cap[1];\n   172\t            if !var_keys.contains(&name) {\n   173\t                return name.to_string();\n   174\t            }\n   175\t        }\n   176\t    }\n   177\t\n   178\t    // Fall back to scanning the entire template\n   179\t    for cap in re.captures_iter(template_source).chain(block_re.captures_iter(template_source)) {\n   180\t        let name = &cap[1];\n   181\t        if !var_keys.contains(&name) Every workstream must respect these. If a change would violate an invariant, it requires explicit discussion and sign-off before proceeding.\n     4\t\n     5\t## I-1: Deterministic Output\n     6\t\n     7\tSame recipe + same variables + same existing files = same output. Always. No randomness, no timestamps, no machine-specific behavior in rendered output. Tests can assert exact equality.\n     8\t\n     9\t## I-2: Idempotent Operations\n    10\t\n    11\tEvery file operation *supports* idempotent re-runs via `skip_if_exists` (create) and `skip_if` (inject). When a recipe is designed for idempotent execution (all creates use `skip_if_exists: true` and all injects use `skip_if`), running the same recipe twice with the same variables produces no changes on the second run. JSON output reports `\"action\": \"skip\"` with a reason for every skipped operation.\n    12\t\n    13\t## I-3: JSON In, Files Out\n    14\t\n    15\tVariables are structured JSON. Output is files on disk. The CLI is non-interactive — no prompts, no wizards, no \"press y to continue.\" An LLM (or script) can call jig without any human in the loop.\n    16\t\n    17\t## I-4: Structured Errors with Rendered Content\n    18\t\n    19\tWhen an operation fails (anchor not found, scope parse fails, file missing), jig still renders the template and includes the rendered content in the error output. The caller never has to re-derive what to insert — only where to put it. Errors include what/where/why + a hint.\n    20\t\n    21\t## I-5: Stable Exit Codes\n    22\t\n    23\tExit codes are API. They do not change between minor versions.\n    24\t\n    25\t| Code | Meaning |\n    26\t|------|---------|\n    27\t| 0 | Success |\n    28\t| 1 | Recipe validation error |\n    29\t| 2 | Template rendering error |\n    30\t| 3 | File operation error |\n    31\t| 4 | Variable validation error |\n    32\t\n    33\t## I-6: Single Static Binary, Zero Runtime Dependencies\n    34\t\n    35\tNo Python, no Node, no JVM. One binary, runs anywhere. Startup must be fast — jig may be called dozens of times in a single LLM session.\n    36\t\n    37\t## I-7: Templates Live With the Consumer\n    38\t\n    39\tThere is no central template directory. Templates are co-located with the recipe that uses them. A recipe + its templates form a self-contained unit that can be moved, versioned, or shared independently.\n    40\t\n    41\t## I-8: Dual Output Streams\n    42\t\n    43\tFor `jig run`: In TTY mode, human-readable colored output to stderr, nothing to stdout. In piped mode, JSON to stdout, nothing to stderr (except errors). `--json` forces JSON to stdout regardless of TTY. `--quiet` suppresses stderr only; stdout behavior is determined by `--json` independently. `--verbose` adds rendered template content to output. Note: `jig vars` and `jig render` write to stdout by default regardless of TTY mode. `jig render --to <path>` redirects output to a file.\n    44\t\n    45\t## I-9: Operations Are Ordered\n    46\t\n    47\tFile operations in a recipe execute in declaration order. Later operations can depend on files created or modified by earlier operations in the same recipe run.\n    48\t\n    49\t## I-10: Graceful Degradation to LLM\n    50\t\n    51\tjig handles the deterministic part (rendering). When structural analysis fails (can't find anchor, can't parse scope), it fails with enough information for the LLM to fall back to its native Edit tool. jig never silently produces wrong output — it either succeeds or fails clearly.\n","exit_code":0,"status":"completed"}}
